<p>In 2012, ABC News and <a href="/wiki/Univision_Communications" title="Univision Communications">Univision Communications</a> announced a partnership to launch an English-language cable news channel primarily aimed at younger English-speaking Hispanics; the new network, <a href="/wiki/Fusion_(TV_channel)" title="Fusion (TV channel)">Fusion</a>, launched on October 28, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> The 2012–13 season failed to live up to the previous year, with only one drama, <i><a href="/wiki/Nashville_(2012_TV_series)" title="Nashville (2012 TV series)">Nashville</a></i>, and one comedy, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Neighbors_(2012_TV_series)" title="The Neighbors (2012 TV series)">The Neighbors</a></i>, earning a second season renewal.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_United_States_network_television_schedule" title="2013–14 United States network television schedule">2013–14 season</a> was a slight improvement for ABC with three new hits in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Goldbergs_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Goldbergs (TV series)">The Goldbergs</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Agents_of_S.H.I.E.L.D." title="Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.">Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Resurrection_(U.S._TV_series)" title="Resurrection (U.S. TV series)">Resurrection</a></i>, all of which were renewed; however, that season saw the cancellations of holdovers <i>The Neighbors</i> (which languished in its new Friday time slot despite being bookended by <i>Last Man Standing</i> and <i>Shark Tank</i>) and <i><a href="/wiki/Suburgatory" title="Suburgatory">Suburgatory</a></i>. NBC, which had lagged behind ABC for eight years, finished the season in first place in the 18–49 demographic for the first time since 2004, and in second place in total viewership behind long-dominant CBS. ABC itself would finish the season in third place as Fox crashed to fourth in both demographics.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_United_States_network_television_schedule" title="2014–15 United States network television schedule">2014–15 season</a> saw moderate hits in <i><a href="/wiki/Black-ish" title="Black-ish">Black-ish</a></i> (the first series on the four major U.S. networks to feature a predominately African-American cast since 2006) and major successes in <i><a href="/wiki/How_to_Get_Away_with_Murder" title="How to Get Away with Murder">How to Get Away with Murder</a></i> (which, alongside <i>Grey's Anatomy</i> and <i>Scandal</i>, became one of the centerpieces of a new Thursday drama lineup, "TGIT", composed of dramas executive produced by <a href="/wiki/Shonda_Rhimes" title="Shonda Rhimes">Shonda Rhimes</a>). New hits came in with fellow new comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Fresh_Off_the_Boat" title="Fresh Off the Boat">Fresh Off the Boat</a></i>, a new drama <i><a href="/wiki/Secrets_and_Lies_(U.S._TV_series)" title="Secrets and Lies (U.S. TV series)">Secrets and Lies</a></i> and a low rated but critically acclaimed show <i><a href="/wiki/American_Crime_(TV_series)" title="American Crime (TV series)">American Crime</a></i>, all of which were renewed. However, that season saw cancellations of <i>Resurrection</i> and <i>Revenge</i>.</p>
<p>By November 2015, ABC was creating a digital slate called internal ABC3 for its WatchABC video streaming app.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> The ABC3 slate of 7 comedy and lifestyle short series debuted under the ABCd banner along with 38 older series under a revamped and renamed ABC app on July 13, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_United_States_network_television_schedule" title="2015–16 United States network television schedule">2015–16 season</a> saw breakout hits such as <i><a href="/wiki/Quantico_(TV_series)" title="Quantico (TV series)">Quantico</a></i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Programming">Programming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Programming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_programs_broadcast_by_American_Broadcasting_Company" title="List of programs broadcast by American Broadcasting Company">List of programs broadcast by American Broadcasting Company</a> and <a href="/wiki/ESPN_on_ABC" title="ESPN on ABC">ESPN on ABC</a></div>
<p>The ABC television network provides 89 hours of regularly scheduled network programming each week. The network provides 22 hours of prime time programming to affiliated stations from 8:00–11:00&#160;p.m. Monday through Saturday (all times Eastern and Pacific Time) and 7:00–11:00&#160;p.m. on Sundays.</p>
<p>Daytime programming is also provided from 11:00&#160;a.m. to 3:00&#160;p.m. weekdays (with a one-hour break at 12:00&#160;p.m. Eastern/Pacific for stations to air newscasts, other locally produced programming such as talk shows, or syndicated programs) featuring the talk/lifestyle shows <i><a href="/wiki/The_View_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The View (U.S. TV series)">The View</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chew" title="The Chew">The Chew</a></i> and the soap opera <i><a href="/wiki/General_Hospital" title="General Hospital">General Hospital</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/ABC_News" title="ABC News">ABC News</a> programming includes <i>Good Morning America</i> from 7:00 to 9:00&#160;a.m. weekdays (along with one-hour weekend editions); nightly editions of <i><a href="/wiki/ABC_World_News_Tonight" title="ABC World News Tonight">ABC World News Tonight</a></i> (whose weekend editions are occasionally subject to abbreviation or preemption due to sports telecasts overrunning into the program's timeslot), the <a href="/wiki/Sunday_morning_talk_shows" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunday morning talk shows">Sunday political talk show</a> <i>This Week</i>, early morning news programs <i><a href="/wiki/World_News_Now" title="World News Now">World News Now</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/America_This_Morning" title="America This Morning">America This Morning</a></i> and the late night newsmagazine <i><a href="/wiki/Nightline" title="Nightline">Nightline</a></i>. Late nights feature the weeknight talk show <i><a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Kimmel_Live!" title="Jimmy Kimmel Live!">Jimmy Kimmel Live!</a></i>.</p>
<p>The network's three-hour Saturday morning children's programming timeslot is programmed by syndication distributor <a href="/wiki/Litton_Entertainment" title="Litton Entertainment">Litton Entertainment</a>, which produces <i><a href="/wiki/Litton%27s_Weekend_Adventure" title="Litton's Weekend Adventure">Litton's Weekend Adventure</a></i> under an arrangement in which the <a href="/wiki/Block_programming" title="Block programming">programming block</a> is syndicated exclusively to ABC owned-and-operated and affiliated stations, rather than being leased out directly by the network to Litton.</p>
<p>Sports programming is also provided on some weekend afternoons at any time from 12:00 to 6:00&#160;p.m. Eastern Time (9:00&#160;a.m. to 3:00&#160;p.m. Pacific) and, during <a href="/wiki/ESPN_College_Football_on_ABC" title="ESPN College Football on ABC">college football</a> season, during prime time on Saturday nights as part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Football" title="Saturday Night Football">Saturday Night Football</a></i> package. Due to the erratic and (outside of <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a> season) highly inconsistent scheduling of sports programming on weekend afternoons since ESPN took over responsibilities for ABC's sports division in 2006, ABC carries the <i><a href="/wiki/ESPN_Sports_Saturday" title="ESPN Sports Saturday">ESPN Sports Saturday</a></i> block on Saturday late afternoons (featuring various ESPN-produced documentaries), and on Sundays either encores of primetime reality series, cancelled series being <a href="/wiki/Burning_off" title="Burning off">burned off</a> that had no room on the primetime schedule, occasional theatrical films which were acquired by the network in the early to mid-2000s that no longer have a primetime slot to air in or more recently, <a href="/wiki/Figure_skating" title="Figure skating">figure skating</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics" title="Gymnastics">gymnastics</a> specials supplied by Disson Skating, when no sports telecasts are scheduled, usually airing between 4:00 and 6:00&#160;p.m. Eastern and Pacific Time. During the summer, ABC airs ESPN-produced highlight compilation programs for <a href="/wiki/The_Open_Championship" title="The Open Championship">The Open Championship</a> golf and <a href="/wiki/The_Championships,_Wimbledon" title="The Championships, Wimbledon">The Wimbledon</a> tennis tournaments to provide some presence for both events on American broadcast television. ABC also carries various <a href="/wiki/X_Games" title="X Games">X Games</a> weekend events not broadcast by ESPN. ABC airs NBA games on Sundays, normally starting in January as "NBA Sunday Showcase" during the regular season, and shows Christmas Day games, regularly between 2–7 PM ET, and NBA playoff games during the weekends, and exclusive rights to the <a href="/wiki/NBA_Finals" title="NBA Finals">NBA Finals</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Daytime">Daytime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Daytime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ABC_Daytime" title="ABC Daytime">ABC Daytime</a></div>
<p>ABC's daytime schedule currently features talk shows <i><a href="/wiki/The_View_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The View (U.S. TV series)">The View</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chew" title="The Chew">The Chew</a></i>, and the soap opera <i><a href="/wiki/General_Hospital" title="General Hospital">General Hospital</a></i>, the latter of which is the longest-running entertainment program in the history of the ABC television network, having aired since 1963. ABC also broadcasts the morning news program <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i> and has done so since 1975, though that program is not considered to be part of the ABC Daytime block. In addition to the long-running <i><a href="/wiki/All_My_Children" title="All My Children">All My Children</a></i> (1970–2011) and <i><a href="/wiki/One_Life_to_Live" title="One Life to Live">One Life to Live</a></i> (1968–2012), notable past soap operas seen on the daytime lineup include <i><a href="/wiki/Ryan%27s_Hope" title="Ryan's Hope">Ryan's Hope</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Shadows" title="Dark Shadows">Dark Shadows</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Loving_(TV_series)" title="Loving (TV series)">Loving</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_City_(1995_TV_series)" title="The City (1995 TV series)">The City</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Port_Charles" title="Port Charles">Port Charles</a></i>. ABC also aired the last nine years of the <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a>-produced soap <i><a href="/wiki/The_Edge_of_Night" title="The Edge of Night">The Edge of Night</a></i>, following its cancellation by CBS in 1975. ABC Daytime has also aired a number of game shows, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dating_Game" title="The Dating Game">The Dating Game</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Newlywed_Game" title="The Newlywed Game">The Newlywed Game</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Make_a_Deal" title="Let's Make a Deal">Let's Make a Deal</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Password_(game_show)" title="Password (game show)">Password</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Split_Second_(game_show)" title="Split Second (game show)">Split Second</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pyramid_(game_show)" title="Pyramid (game show)">The $10,000/$20,000 Pyramid</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Family_Feud" title="Family Feud">Family Feud</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Better_Sex" title="The Better Sex">The Better Sex</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Trivia_Trap" title="Trivia Trap">Trivia Trap</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/All-Star_Blitz" title="All-Star Blitz">All-Star Blitz</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Bruce_Forsyth%27s_Hot_Streak" title="Bruce Forsyth's Hot Streak">Hot Streak</a></i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Specials">Specials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Specials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>ABC currently holds the broadcast rights to the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a>, Emmy Awards (which are rotated across all four major networks on a year-to-year basis), <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Award" title="American Music Award">American Music Awards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Parks_Christmas_Day_Parade" title="Disney Parks Christmas Day Parade">Disney Parks Christmas Day Parade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rose_Parade" title="Rose Parade">Tournament of Roses Parade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association_Awards" title="Country Music Association Awards">Country Music Association Awards</a> and the <a href="/wiki/CMA_Music_Festival" title="CMA Music Festival">CMA Music Festival</a>. Since 2000, ABC has also owned the television rights to most of the <i><a href="/wiki/Peanuts" title="Peanuts">Peanuts</a></i> television specials, having acquired the broadcast rights from CBS, which originated the specials in 1965 with the debut of <i><a href="/wiki/A_Charlie_Brown_Christmas" title="A Charlie Brown Christmas">A Charlie Brown Christmas</a></i> (other <i>Peanuts</i> specials broadcast annually by ABC, including <i>A Charlie Brown Christmas</i>, include <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_the_Great_Pumpkin,_Charlie_Brown" title="It's the Great Pumpkin, Charlie Brown">It's the Great Pumpkin, Charlie Brown</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/A_Charlie_Brown_Thanksgiving" title="A Charlie Brown Thanksgiving">A Charlie Brown Thanksgiving</a></i>).</p>
<p>Since 1974, ABC has generally aired <i><a href="/wiki/Dick_Clark%27s_New_Year%27s_Rockin%27_Eve" title="Dick Clark's New Year's Rockin' Eve">Dick Clark's New Year's Rockin' Eve</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve" title="New Year's Eve">New Year's Eve</a> (hosted first by its creator Dick Clark, and later by his successor <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Seacrest" title="Ryan Seacrest">Ryan Seacrest</a>); the only exception was in 1999, when ABC put it on a one-year hiatus to provide <a href="/wiki/ABC_2000" class="mw-redirect" title="ABC 2000">coverage of the international millennium festivities</a>, though Clark's traditional countdown from Times Square was still featured within the coverage. ABC has also aired the <a href="/wiki/Miss_America" title="Miss America">Miss America</a> pageant from 1954 to 1956, 1997 to 2005 (with the television rights being assumed by cable channel <a href="/wiki/TLC_(TV_network)" title="TLC (TV network)">TLC</a> in 2006, when the pageant moved from its longtime homebase in <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City,_New_Jersey" title="Atlantic City, New Jersey">Atlantic City</a> to <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas</a>, before returning to Atlantic City in 2013) and since 2011. Under its current contract with the <a href="/wiki/Miss_America_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Miss America Organization">Miss America Organization</a>, ABC will continue to broadcast the pageant through 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, ABC began airing the <a href="/wiki/ESPY_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="ESPY Awards">ESPY Awards</a> show, which normally aired on ESPN before 2015. In the ABC debut of the ESPY's, <a href="/wiki/Caitlyn_Jenner" title="Caitlyn Jenner">Caitlyn Jenner</a> was awarded the Arthur Ash Award for courage, after she announced in a 20/20 interview, that she was becoming transgender.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Programming_library">Programming library</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Programming library">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>ABC owns nearly all its in-house television and theatrical productions made from the 1970s onward, with the exception of certain co-productions with producers (for example, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Commish" title="The Commish">The Commish</a></i> is now owned by the estate of its producer, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_J._Cannell" title="Stephen J. Cannell">Stephen Cannell</a>). Worldwide video rights are currently owned by various companies, for example, <a href="/wiki/MGM_Home_Entertainment" title="MGM Home Entertainment">MGM Home Entertainment</a> via <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox_Home_Entertainment" title="20th Century Fox Home Entertainment">20th Century Fox Home Entertainment</a> owns U.S. video rights to many of ABC's feature films.</p>
<p>When the FCC imposed its <a href="/wiki/Financial_Interest_and_Syndication_Rules" title="Financial Interest and Syndication Rules">fin-syn</a> rules in 1970, ABC proactively created two companies: Worldvision Enterprises as a syndication distributor, and ABC Circle Films as a production company. However, between the publication and implementation of these regulations, the separation of the network's catalog was made in 1973. The broadcast rights to pre-1973 productions were transferred to Worldvision, which became independent in the same year. The company has been sold several times since <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Television" title="Paramount Television">Paramount Television</a> acquired it in 1999, and has most recently been absorbed into <a href="/wiki/CBS_Television_Distribution" title="CBS Television Distribution">CBS Television Distribution</a>, a unit of <a href="/wiki/CBS_Corporation" title="CBS Corporation">CBS Corporation</a>. Nonetheless, Worldvision sold portions of its catalog, including the <a href="/wiki/Ruby-Spears" title="Ruby-Spears">Ruby-Spears</a> and Hanna-Barbera libraries, to <a href="/wiki/Turner_Broadcasting_System" title="Turner Broadcasting System">Turner Broadcasting System</a> in 1991. With Disney's 1996 purchase of ABC, ABC Circle Films was absorbed into Touchstone Television, a Disney subsidiary which in turn was renamed ABC Studios in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-WDC-ABC_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WDC-ABC-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also part of the library are most films in the <a href="/wiki/David_O._Selznick" title="David O. Selznick">David O. Selznick</a> library, the <a href="/wiki/Cinerama_Productions" class="mw-redirect" title="Cinerama Productions">Cinerama Productions</a>/Palomar theatrical library (with the exception of those films produced in Cinerama which are now under the control of <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Theatres" title="Pacific Theatres">Pacific Theatres</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Flicker_Alley&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Flicker Alley (page does not exist)">Flicker Alley</a>), the Selmur Productions catalog that the network acquired some years back, and the in-house productions it continues to produce (such as <i><a href="/wiki/America%27s_Funniest_Home_Videos" title="America's Funniest Home Videos">America's Funniest Home Videos</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Grey%27s_Anatomy" title="Grey's Anatomy">Grey's Anatomy</a></i>, <i>General Hospital</i>, and ABC News productions), although <a href="/wiki/Disney%E2%80%93ABC_Domestic_Television" title="Disney–ABC Domestic Television">Disney–ABC Domestic Television</a> (formerly known as Buena Vista Television) handles domestic television distribution, while <a href="/wiki/Disney_Media_Distribution" title="Disney Media Distribution">Disney–ABC International Television</a> (formerly known as Buena Vista International Television) handles international television distribution.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stations">Stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_ABC_television_affiliates_(by_U.S._state)" title="List of ABC television affiliates (by U.S. state)">List of ABC television affiliates (by U.S. state)</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_ABC_television_affiliates_(table)" title="List of ABC television affiliates (table)">List of ABC television affiliates (table)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ABC_Owned_Television_Stations" title="ABC Owned Television Stations">ABC Owned Television Stations</a></div>
<p>Since its inception, ABC has had many affiliated stations, which include WABC-TV and WPVI-TV, the first two stations to carry the network's programming. As of March 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, ABC has eight owned-and-operated stations, and current and pending affiliation agreements with 235 additional television stations encompassing 49 states, the District of Columbia, four U.S. possessions, <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-re_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-re-187">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-StationIndex_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StationIndex-188">[188]</a></sup> this makes ABC the largest U.S. broadcast television network by total number of affiliates. The network has an estimated national reach of 96.26% of all households in the United States (or 300,794,157 Americans with at least one television set).</p>
<p>Currently, <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> are the only U.S. states where ABC does not have a locally licensed affiliate (New Jersey is served by New York City O&amp;O WABC-TV and Philadelphia O&amp;O WPVI-TV; Rhode Island is served by <a href="/wiki/New_Bedford,_Massachusetts" title="New Bedford, Massachusetts">New Bedford, Massachusetts</a>-licensed <a href="/wiki/WLNE-TV" title="WLNE-TV">WLNE</a>; and Delaware is served by WPVI and <a href="/wiki/Salisbury,_Maryland" title="Salisbury, Maryland">Salisbury, Maryland</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WMDT" title="WMDT">WMDT</a>). ABC maintains affiliations with low-power stations (broadcasting either in analog or digital) in a few markets, such as <a href="/wiki/Birmingham,_Alabama" title="Birmingham, Alabama">Birmingham, Alabama</a> (<a href="/wiki/WBMA-LD" title="WBMA-LD">WBMA-LD</a>), <a href="/wiki/Lima,_Ohio" title="Lima, Ohio">Lima, Ohio</a> (<a href="/wiki/WLQP-LP" title="WLQP-LP">WLQP-LP</a>) and <a href="/wiki/South_Bend,_Indiana" title="South Bend, Indiana">South Bend, Indiana</a> (<a href="/wiki/WBND-LD" title="WBND-LD">WBND-LD</a>). In some markets, including the former two mentioned, these stations also maintain digital simulcasts on a subchannel of a co-owned/co-managed full-power television station.</p>
<p>The network has the unusual distinction of having separately owned and operated affiliates which serve the same market in <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">Tampa, Florida</a> (WFTS-TV and <a href="/wiki/WWSB" title="WWSB">WWSB</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Grand_Rapids,_Michigan" title="Grand Rapids, Michigan">Grand Rapids, Michigan</a> (<a href="/wiki/WZZM" title="WZZM">WZZM</a> and <a href="/wiki/WOTV" title="WOTV">WOTV</a>), with an analogous situation arising in <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City,_Missouri" title="Kansas City, Missouri">Kansas City, Missouri</a> (<a href="/wiki/KMBC-TV" title="KMBC-TV">KMBC-TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/KQTV" title="KQTV">KQTV</a>). KQTV is licensed to <a href="/wiki/St._Joseph,_Missouri" title="St. Joseph, Missouri">St. Joseph, Missouri</a>, which is designated by <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_Holdings" title="Nielsen Holdings">Nielsen</a> as a separate market from Kansas City despite being located within 55 miles (89&#160;km) of one another, while WWSB and WOTV serve areas that do not receive an adequate signal from their market's primary ABC affiliate (in the case of WWSB, this dates back to when <a href="/wiki/WTSP" title="WTSP">WTSP</a> was Tampa's primary ABC affiliate prior to 1994, with the former being necessitated to serve the southern part of the Tampa market including the station's <a href="/wiki/City_of_license" title="City of license">city of license</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarasota,_Florida" title="Sarasota, Florida">Sarasota</a>, due to WTSP's transmitter being short-spaced to avoid interfering with the analog signal of <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WPLG" title="WPLG">WPLG</a> – which like WTSP, broadcast on VHF channel 10).</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sinclair_Broadcast_Group" title="Sinclair Broadcast Group">Sinclair Broadcast Group</a> is the largest operator of ABC stations by numerical total, owning or providing services to 28 ABC affiliates and two additional subchannel-only affiliates; Sinclair owns the largest ABC subchannel affiliate by market size, <a href="/wiki/WABM" title="WABM">WABM-DT2</a>/<a href="/wiki/WTTO" title="WTTO">WDBB-DT2</a> in the Birmingham market, which serve as repeaters of WBMA-LD (which itself is also simulcast on a subchannel of former WBMA satellite <a href="/wiki/WGWW" title="WGWW">WGWW</a>, owned by Sinclair partner company <a href="/wiki/Armstrong_Williams#Howard_Stirk_Holdings" title="Armstrong Williams">Howard Stirk Holdings</a>). The <a href="/wiki/E._W._Scripps_Company" title="E. W. Scripps Company">E. W. Scripps Company</a> is the largest operator of ABC stations in terms of overall market reach, owning 15 ABC-affiliated stations (including affiliates in larger markets such as <a href="/wiki/WEWS" class="mw-redirect" title="WEWS">Cleveland</a>, <a href="/wiki/KNXV-TV" title="KNXV-TV">Phoenix</a>, <a href="/wiki/WXYZ-TV" title="WXYZ-TV">Detroit</a> and <a href="/wiki/KMGH-TV" title="KMGH-TV">Denver</a>), and through its ownership of <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix</a> affiliate KNXV, <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/KTNV-TV" title="KTNV-TV">KTNV-TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tucson,_Arizona" title="Tucson, Arizona">Tucson</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/KGUN-TV" title="KGUN-TV">KGUN-TV</a>, the only provider of ABC programming for the majority of <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> (outside of the <a href="/wiki/Yuma,_Arizona" title="Yuma, Arizona">Yuma</a>-<a href="/wiki/El_Centro,_California" title="El Centro, California">El Centro</a> market) and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Nevada" title="Southern Nevada">Southern Nevada</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities_and_studios">Facilities and studios</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Facilities and studios">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>All of ABC's owned-and-operated stations and affiliates have had their own facilities and studios, but transverse entities have been created to produce national programming. As a result, television series were produced by ABC Circle Films beginning in 1962 and by Touchstone Television beginning in 1985, before Touchstone was reorganized as <a href="/wiki/ABC_Studios" title="ABC Studios">ABC Studios</a> in February 2007. Since the 1950s, ABC has had two main production facilities: the ABC Television Center (now The Prospect Studios) on <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Boulevard" title="Hollywood Boulevard">Prospect Avenue</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hollywood,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Hollywood, California">Hollywood, California</a>, shared with the operations of KABC-TV until 1999; and the ABC Television Center, East, a set of studios located throughout the New York City.</p>
<p>ABC owns several facilities in New York grouped mainly on West 66th Street. The main set of facilities is on the corner of Columbus Avenue and West 66th Street. In total, ABC's facilities occupy a combined 9,755 square meters (105,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) of the 14,864 square meters (159,990&#160;sq&#160;ft) of the blocks they encompass. The aforementioned set includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>The official headquarters at 77 West 66th Street, a 22-story building built in 1988 on a 175 feet (53&#160;m) × 200 feet (61&#160;m) plot;</li>
<li>A pair of buildings at 149–155 Columbus Avenue (with one building comprising 10 stories and the other seven, and both containing glass bays connecting them to each other), constructed on a 100 feet (30&#160;m) × 200 feet (61&#160;m) plot;</li>
<li>30–34 West 67th Street, a 15-story building with a facade on the 66th and 67th Street on a 100 feet (30&#160;m) × 100 feet (30&#160;m) plot;</li>
<li>The former First Battery of New York National Guard, a five-story building located at number 56 on the other side of the street, on a 174 feet (53&#160;m) × 100 feet (30&#160;m) plot;</li>
<li>ABC also owns 47 West 66th Street, one of three 14-story buildings on a 375 feet (114&#160;m) x 100 feet (30&#160;m) plot. From 1983 to 2013, Disney leased 70,000 square feet (6,500&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) at 157 Columbus Avenue, just on the other side of 67th Street.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<p>ABC also owns the <a href="/wiki/Times_Square_Studios" title="Times Square Studios">Times Square Studios</a> at 1500 Broadway on land in <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a> owned by a development fund for the <a href="/wiki/42nd_Street_(Manhattan)" title="42nd Street (Manhattan)">42nd Street</a> Project; opened in 1999, <i>Good Morning America</i> and <i>Nightline</i> are broadcast from this particular facility. ABC News has premises a little further on West 66th Street, in a six-story building occupying a 196 feet (60&#160;m) × 379 feet (116&#160;m) plot at 121–135 <a href="/wiki/West_End_Avenue" class="mw-redirect" title="West End Avenue">West End Avenue</a>. The block of West 66th street between Central Park West and Columbus Ave which houses the ABC News building was renamed <i>Peter Jennings Way</i> in 2006 in honor of the recently deceased longtime ABC News chief anchor and anchor of <i>World News Tonight</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_services">Related services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Related services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video-on-demand_services">Video-on-demand services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Video-on-demand services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>ABC maintains several <a href="/wiki/Video_on_demand" title="Video on demand">video on demand</a> services for delayed viewing of the network's programming, including a traditional VOD service called ABC on Demand, which is carried on most traditional cable and <a href="/wiki/IPTV" title="IPTV">IPTV</a> providers. The Walt Disney Company is also a part-owner of <a href="/wiki/Hulu" title="Hulu">Hulu</a> (as part of a consortium that includes, among other parties, the respective parent companies of NBC and Fox, <a href="/wiki/NBCUniversal" title="NBCUniversal">NBCUniversal</a> and <a href="/wiki/21st_Century_Fox" title="21st Century Fox">21st Century Fox</a>), and has offered full-length episodes of most of ABC's programming through the <a href="/wiki/Streaming_media" title="Streaming media">streaming</a> service since July 6, 2009 (which are available for viewing on Hulu's website and <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">mobile app</a>, and since July 2016, through <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_View" title="Yahoo! View">Yahoo! View</a> as part of Hulu's spin-off of their free service to Yahoo),<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> as part of an agreement reached in April that year that also allowed Disney to acquire a 27% ownership stake in Hulu.</p>
<p>In May 2013, ABC launched "WATCH ABC", a revamp of its traditional multi-platform streaming services encompassing the network's existing streaming portal at ABC.com and a <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">mobile app</a> for <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablet computers</a>; in addition to providing full-length episodes of ABC programs, the service allows live programming streams of local ABC affiliates in select markets (the first such offering by a U.S. broadcast network). Similar to sister network ESPN's <a href="/wiki/WatchESPN" title="WatchESPN">WatchESPN</a> service (which originated the "WATCH" brand used by the streaming services of Disney's television networks), live streams of ABC stations are only available to <a href="/wiki/TV_Everywhere" title="TV Everywhere">authenticated subscribers of participating pay television providers</a> in certain markets. New York City O&amp;O WABC-TV and Philadelphia O&amp;O WPVI-TV were the first stations to offer streams of their programming on the service (with a <a href="/wiki/Free_preview" title="Free preview">free preview</a> for non-subscribers through June 2013), with the six remaining ABC O&amp;Os offering streams by the start of the 2013–14 season. <a href="/wiki/Hearst_Television" title="Hearst Television">Hearst Television</a> also reached a deal to offer streams of its ABC affiliates (including stations in <a href="/wiki/WCVB-TV" title="WCVB-TV">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/KMBC-TV" title="KMBC-TV">Kansas City</a>, <a href="/wiki/WISN-TV" title="WISN-TV">Milwaukee</a> and <a href="/wiki/WPBF-TV" class="mw-redirect" title="WPBF-TV">West Palm Beach</a>) on the service, though as of 2016 these stations are only available for live-streaming for <a href="/wiki/DirecTV" title="DirecTV">DirecTV</a> subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-variety-watchabc_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety-watchabc-192">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-engadget-watchabc_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-engadget-watchabc-193">[193]</a></sup></p>
<p>The most recent episodes of the network's shows are usually made available on WATCH ABC, Hulu and ABC on Demand the day after their original broadcast. In addition, ABC on Demand (like the video-on-demand television services provided by the other U.S. broadcast networks) disallows <a href="/wiki/Fast_forward" title="Fast forward">fast forwarding</a> of accessed content. Restrictions implemented by Disney–ABC Television Group on January 7, 2014 restrict streaming of the most recent episode of any ABC program on Hulu and WATCH ABC until eight days after their initial broadcast, in order to encourage live or same-week (via both <a href="/wiki/Digital_video_recorder" title="Digital video recorder">DVR</a> and cable on demand) viewing, with day-after-air streaming on either service limited to subscribers of participating pay television providers (such as <a href="/wiki/Comcast" title="Comcast">Comcast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Verizon_FiOS" class="mw-redirect" title="Verizon FiOS">Verizon FiOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner_Cable" title="Time Warner Cable">Time Warner Cable</a>) using an <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">ISP</a> account via an authenticated user login.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ABC_HD">ABC HD</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: ABC HD">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ABC_HD_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/ABC_HD_logo.png/220px-ABC_HD_logo.png" width="220" height="95" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/ABC_HD_logo.png/330px-ABC_HD_logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/aa/ABC_HD_logo.png 2x" data-file-width="362" data-file-height="156" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ABC_HD_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Logo for ABC HD.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>ABC's master feed is transmitted in <a href="/wiki/720p" title="720p">720p</a> <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">high definition</a>, the native resolution format for The Walt Disney Company's U.S. television properties. However, most of Hearst Television's 16 ABC-affiliated stations transmit the network's programming in <a href="/wiki/1080i" title="1080i">1080i</a> HD, while 11 other affiliates owned by various companies carry the network feed in <a href="/wiki/480i" title="480i">480i</a> <a href="/wiki/Standard-definition_television" title="Standard-definition television">standard definition</a><sup id="cite_ref-re_187-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-re-187">[187]</a></sup> either due to technical considerations for affiliates of other major networks that carry ABC programming on a digital subchannel or because a primary feed ABC affiliate has not yet upgraded their transmission equipment to allow content to be presented in HD.</p>
<p>ABC began its conversion to <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">high definition</a> with the launch of its simulcast feed, ABC HD, on September 16, 2001 at the start of the <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_United_States_network_television_schedule" title="2001–02 United States network television schedule">2001–02 season</a>, with its scripted prime time series becoming the first shows to upgrade to the format. The network's slate of freshmen scripted series were broadcast in HD from their debuts, while all scripted series held over from the <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_United_States_network_television_schedule" title="2000–01 United States network television schedule">2000–01 season</a> were converted from <a href="/wiki/Standard-definition_television" title="Standard-definition television">standard-definition</a> to high definition beginning that season.</p>
<p>With the 2011 cancellation of <i><a href="/wiki/Supernanny" title="Supernanny">Supernanny</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Extreme_Makeover:_Home_Edition" title="Extreme Makeover: Home Edition">Extreme Makeover: Home Edition</a></i> became the only remaining program on the network's schedule that was broadcast in <a href="/wiki/4:3" class="mw-redirect" title="4:3">4:3</a> standard definition. All of the network's programming has been presented in HD since January 2012 (with the exception of certain <a href="/wiki/Christmas_holiday_season" class="mw-redirect" title="Christmas holiday season">holiday</a> specials produced prior to 2005 – such as the <i>Peanuts</i> specials and <i><a href="/wiki/Rudolph%27s_Shiny_New_Year" title="Rudolph's Shiny New Year">Rudolph's Shiny New Year</a></i> – which continue to be presented in 4:3 SD), when <i>Extreme Makeover: Home Edition</i> ended its run as a regular series and <i>One Life to Live</i> (which had been presented in <a href="/wiki/16:9" title="16:9">16:9</a> standard definition since 2010) also ended its ABC run. The affiliate-syndicated Saturday morning E/I block <i>Litton's Weekend Aventure</i> is also broadcast in HD, and was the first children's program block on any U.S. broadcast network to feature programs available in the format upon its September 2011 debut.</p>
<p>On September 1, 2016, ABC began to use <a href="/wiki/16:9" title="16:9">16:9</a> framing for all of most graphical imaging (primarily the network's logo bug, in-program promotions and generic closing credit sequences as well as sports telecasts, where the BottomLine and scoreboard elements now extend outside the 4:3 frame), requiring its stations and pay television providers to display its programming in a compulsory <a href="/wiki/Widescreen" title="Widescreen">widescreen</a> format, either in high definition or standard definition; with the change, some programs (such as <i>Grey's Anatomy</i>, <i>The Goldbergs</i> and <i>Quantico</i>) also began positioning their main on-screen credits outside of the 4:3 aspect ratio. This leaves <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_CW" title="The CW">The CW</a> as the last two major networks to continue to prefer 4:3 framing for graphics.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis">Analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since its inception, the American Broadcasting Company has evolved with the development of various assets, many of which have been sold. The company originates from a radio network that went on the air in 1927, was forced by law to separate from its original parent company, and then became an independent company. The new company diversified rapidly in the emerging medium of television.</p>
<p>The company diversified again through its mergers with United Paramount Theatres in 1950 and later with Capital Cities in 1985. Under UPT, ABC was a sister company to a large theater chain, while under Capital Cities, it was a sister company to various publications. However, ABC was separated from its theaters by the time of the Capital Cities merger, and from its sister newspapers during Disney's purchase of the network in 1996.</p>
<p>A 1993 annual corporate report indicated that 70% of Capital Cities/ABC's revenue came from the sale of advertising space, and for the rest, the two main positions were subscriptions to pay television channels and direct sales of books and journals.<sup id="cite_ref-Annual1993_141-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Annual1993-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_identity">Visual identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Visual identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:American_Broadcasting_Company_Logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/American_Broadcasting_Company_Logo.svg/150px-American_Broadcasting_Company_Logo.svg.png" width="150" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/American_Broadcasting_Company_Logo.svg/225px-American_Broadcasting_Company_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/American_Broadcasting_Company_Logo.svg/300px-American_Broadcasting_Company_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="513" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:American_Broadcasting_Company_Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The "ABC Circle" logo, designed by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rand" title="Paul Rand">Paul Rand</a> in 1962</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The ABC logo has evolved many times since the network's creation in 1943. The network's first logo, introduced in 1946, consisted of a television screen containing the letters "T" and "V", with a vertical <i>ABC</i> microphone in the center,<sup id="cite_ref-logo_evolution_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-logo_evolution-194">[194]</a></sup> referencing the network's roots in radio. When the ABC-UPT merger was finalized in 1953, the network introduced a new logo based on the seal of the Federal Communications Commission, with the letters "ABC" enclosed in a circular <a href="/wiki/Heraldry" title="Heraldry">shield</a> surmounted by the <a href="/wiki/Bald_eagle" title="Bald eagle">bald eagle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-logo_evolution_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-logo_evolution-194">[194]</a></sup> In 1957, just before the television network began its first color broadcasts, the ABC logo consisted of a tiny lowercase "abc" in the center of a large lowercase letter <i>a</i>, a design known as the "ABC Circle A".<sup id="cite_ref-logo_evolution_194-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-logo_evolution-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1962, graphic designer <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rand" title="Paul Rand">Paul Rand</a> redesigned the ABC logo into its best-known (and current) form, with the lowercase letters "abc" enclosed in a single black circle. The new logo debuted on-air for ABC's promos at the start of the 1963–64 season. The letters are strongly reminiscent of the <a href="/wiki/Bauhaus_(typeface)" title="Bauhaus (typeface)">Bauhaus</a> typeface designed by <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Bayer" title="Herbert Bayer">Herbert Bayer</a> in the 1920s,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGernsheimer201043_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGernsheimer201043-195">[195]</a></sup> but also share similarities with several other fonts, such as <a href="/wiki/ITC_Avant_Garde" title="ITC Avant Garde">ITC Avant Garde</a> and Horatio, and most closely resembling Chalet. The logo's simplicity made it easier to redesign and duplicate, which conferred a benefit for ABC (mostly before the advent of <a href="/wiki/Computer_graphics" title="Computer graphics">computer graphics</a>).</p>
<p>The 1970s and 1980s saw the emergence of many graphical imaging packages for the network which based the logo's setting mainly on special lighting effects then under development including white, blue, pink, rainbow neon and glittering dotted lines. Among the "ABC Circle" logo's many variants was a 1977 ID sequence that featured a bubble on a black background representing the circle with glossy gold letters, and as such, was the first ABC identification card to have a three-dimensional appearance.<sup id="cite_ref-logo_evolution_194-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-logo_evolution-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1983, for the 40th anniversary of the network's founding, ID sequences had the logo appear in a gold <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">CGI</a> design on a blue background, accompanied by the slogan "That Special Feeling" in a script font.<sup id="cite_ref-logo_evolution_194-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-logo_evolution-194">[194]</a></sup> Ten years later, in 1993, the "ABC Circle" logo reverted to its classic white-on-black color scheme, but with gloss effects on both the circle and the letters, and a bronze border surrounding the circle.<sup id="cite_ref-logo_evolution_194-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-logo_evolution-194">[194]</a></sup> The ABC logo first appeared as a <a href="/wiki/Digital_on-screen_graphic" title="Digital on-screen graphic">on-screen bug</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_United_States_network_television_schedule" title="1993–94 United States network television schedule">1993–94 season</a>, appearing initially only for 60 seconds at the beginning of an act or segment, before appearing throughout programs (except during commercial breaks) beginning in the <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_United_States_network_television_schedule" title="1997–98 United States network television schedule">1995–96 season</a>; the respective iterations of the translucent logo bug were also incorporated within program promotions until the 2011–12 season.</p>
<p>In 1998, the network began using a minimalist graphical identity, designed by Pittard Sullivan, featuring a small black-and-white "ABC Circle" logo on a yellow background (promotions during this time also featured a sequence of still photos of the stars of its programs during the timeslot card as well as the schedule sequence that began each night's prime time lineup).<sup id="cite_ref-logo_evolution_194-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-logo_evolution-194">[194]</a></sup> A new four-note theme tune was introduced alongside the package, based around the network's "We Love TV" image campaign introduced that year, creating an audio signature on par with the <a href="/wiki/NBC_chimes" title="NBC chimes">NBC chimes</a>, CBS' various three-note soundmarks (including the current version used since 1992) and the <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox#Logo_and_fanfare" title="20th Century Fox">Fox Fanfare</a>. The four-note signature has been updated with every television season thereafter (though variants of it used since the <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_United_States_network_television_schedule" title="1998–99 United States network television schedule">1998–99 season</a> remain in use during the production company vanity cards shown following the closing credits of most programs). In the fall of 2015, ABC stopped with its 1998–2002 four-note jingles for the production company vanity cards following the closing credits of most of its programs over seventeen years; now it has a different and adventure-type music, including the drums or the chorus of the network's four-note signature. Also, a new music (since 2015) is also heard on the network's tonight lineup and the intros for each ABC show.</p>
<p>In 2000, ABC launched a web-based promotional campaign focused around its circle logo, also called "the dot", in which comic book character <a href="/wiki/Little_Dot" title="Little Dot">Little Dot</a> prompted visitors to "download the dot", a program which would cause the ABC logo to fly around the screen and settle in the bottom-right corner.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-196">[196]</a></sup> The network hired the <a href="/wiki/Troika_Design_Group" title="Troika Design Group">Troika Design Group</a> to design and produce its 2001–02 identity, which continued using the black-and-yellow coloring of the logo and featured dots and stripes in various promotional and identification spots.<sup id="cite_ref-InsideDesign_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InsideDesign-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 16, 2007, ABC began to phase in a new imaging campaign for the upcoming 2007–08 season, "Start Here". Also developed by Troika, the on-air design was intended to emphasize the availability of ABC content across multiple platforms (in particular, using a system of icons representing different devices, such as television, computers and mobile devices), and "simplify and bring a lot more consistency and continuity to the visual representation of ABC". The ABC logo was also significantly redesigned as part of the transition, with a glossy "ball" effect that was specifically designed for HD. On-air, the logo was accompanied by animated water and ribbon effects. Red ribbons were used to represent the entertainment division, while blue ribbons were used for ABC News.<sup id="cite_ref-abcnews-starthere_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abcnews-starthere-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tvw-starthere_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tvw-starthere-198">[198]</a></sup></p>
<p>A revised version of the ABC logo was introduced for promotions for the 2013–14 season during the network's <a href="/wiki/Upfront_(advertising)" title="Upfront (advertising)">upfront</a> presentation on May 14, 2013, and officially introduced on-air on May 30 (although some affiliates implemented the new design prior to then), as part of an overhaul of ABC's identity by design agency LoyalKaspar. The updated logo carries a simpler gloss design than the previous version, and contains lettering more closely resembling Paul Rand's original version of the circle logo. The logo is displayed on-air, online and in print advertising in four variants shading the respective color used with the circle design's native black coloring: a gold version is primarily used on entertainment-oriented outlets (such as ABC.com, WATCH ABC, and by ABC Studios) and the on-screen bug; steel blue and dark grey versions are used primarily by ABC News; a red version is used for <a href="/wiki/ESPN_on_ABC" title="ESPN on ABC">ESPN on ABC</a>, while all four variants are used selectively in advertising and by affiliates. A new custom <a href="/wiki/Typeface" title="Typeface">typeface</a>, "ABC Modern" (which was inspired by the logotype), was also created for use in advertising and other promotional materials.<sup id="cite_ref-lk-abc_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lk-abc-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_development">International development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: International development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first attempts to internationalize the ABC television network date back to the 1950s, after Leonard Goldenson, following the United Paramount Theatres model, tried to use on ABC the same strategies he had made in expanding UPT's theater operation to the international market.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993214_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993214-200">[200]</a></sup> Leonard Goldenson said that ABC's first international activity was broadcasting the coronation of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> in June 1953; CBS and NBC were unable to cover the coronation live due to respective issues with technical problems and flight delays.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993215.E2.80.93216_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993215.E2.80.93216-201">[201]</a></sup> NBC's plane landed in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(geographic_names)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (geographic names)"><span title="The geographic scope near this tag is ambiguous. (January 2016)">where?</span></a></i>]</sup>, leading ABC to learn of subsidiaries in that region.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993215.E2.80.93216_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993215.E2.80.93216-201">[201]</a></sup> Goldenson tried international investing, having ABC invest in the Latin American market, acquiring a 51% interest in a network covering <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993217_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993217-202">[202]</a></sup> Goldenson also cited interest in Japan in the early 1950s,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993221_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993221-203">[203]</a></sup> acquiring a 5% stake in two new domestic networks, the <a href="/wiki/Mainichi_Broadcasting_System" title="Mainichi Broadcasting System">Mainichi Broadcasting System</a> in 1951 and <a href="/wiki/Nihon_Educational_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Nihon Educational Television">Nihon Educational Television</a> in 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993221_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993221-203">[203]</a></sup> Goldenson also invested in broadcasting properties in <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a> in the mid-1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993223_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993223-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<p>The idea was to create a network of wholly and partially owned channels, and affiliates to rebroadcast the network's programs. In 1959, this rerun activity was completed with program syndication, with ABC Films selling programs to networks not owned by ABC.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993227_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993227-205">[205]</a></sup> The arrival of satellite television ended the need for ABC to hold interests in other countries;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993231_110-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993231-110">[110]</a></sup> many governments also wanted to increase their independence and strengthen legislation to limit foreign ownership of broadcasting properties. As a result, ABC was forced to sell all of its interests in international networks, mainly in Japan and Latin America, in the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993232_70-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldensonWolf1991.E2.80.931993232-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>A second period of international expansion is linked to that of the ESPN network in the 1990s, and policies enacted in the 2000s by Disney Media Networks (which included the expansion of several of the company's U.S.-based cable networks including Disney Channel and its spinoffs Toon Disney, <a href="/wiki/Playhouse_Disney" title="Playhouse Disney">Playhouse Disney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jetix" title="Jetix">Jetix</a>; although Disney also sold its 33% stake in European sports channel <a href="/wiki/Eurosport" title="Eurosport">Eurosport</a> for $155 million in June 2000<sup id="cite_ref-Annual_2000_p65_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Annual_2000_p65-206">[206]</a></sup>). In contrast to Disney's other channels, ABC is broadcast in the United States, although the network's programming is syndicated in many countries. The policy regarding wholly owned international networks was revived in 2004 when on September 27 of that year, ABC announced the launch of <a href="/wiki/ABC1_(UK)" title="ABC1 (UK)">ABC1</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Free-to-air" title="Free-to-air">free-to-air</a> channel in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> owned by the ABC Group.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2004_9_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook_2004_9-207">[207]</a></sup> However, on September 8, 2007, Disney announced that it would discontinue ABC1 citing to the channel's inability to attain sustainable viewership.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC1_closure_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC1_closure-208">[208]</a></sup> With ABC1's shutdown that October, the company's attempt to develop ABC International were discontinued.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC1_closure_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC1_closure-208">[208]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prior to the ABC1 closure, on October 10, 2006, Disney–ABC Television Group entered into an agreement with satellite provider <a href="/wiki/Dish_TV" title="Dish TV">Dish TV</a> to carry its ABC News Now channel in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DishTv_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DishTv-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Movies_produced_by_ABC_or_its_divisions">Movies produced by ABC or its divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Broadcasting_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Movies produced by ABC or its divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

			<h2>Navigation menu</h2>

			<div id="mw-head">
									<div id="p-personal" role="navigation" class="" aria-labelledby="p-personal-label">
